        // Now submit the form. WebDriver will find the form for us from the element
        element.submit();
        // Check the title of the page
        System.out.println("Page title is: " + driver.getTitle());
        // Googles search is rendered dynamically with JavaScript.
        // Wait for the page to load, timeout after 10 seconds
        (new WebDriverWait(driver, 10)).until(new ExpectedCondition&lt;Boolean&gt;() {
            public Boolean apply(WebDriver d) {
                return d.getTitle().toLowerCase().startsWith("cheese!");
            }
        });
        // Should see: "cheese! - Google Search"
        System.out.println("Page title is: " + driver.getTitle());
        //Close the browser
        driver.quit();

      (11,jayes,trainee)";
      String insertEmp3 = "insert into emp values
      (12,shail,trainee)";
      con.setAutoCommit(false);
      stmt.addBatch(insertEmp1);
      stmt.addBatch(insertEmp2);
      stmt.addBatch(insertEmp3);
      ResultSet rs = stmt.executeQuery("select * from emp");
      rs.last();
      System.out.println("rows before batch execution= "
      + rs.getRow());
      stmt.executeBatch();
      con.commit();
      System.out.println("Batch executed");
      rs = stmt.executeQuery("select * from emp");
      rs.last();
      System.out.println("rows after batch execution= "
      + rs.getRow());
   }
} 
</code></pre>
<p><strong>Result:</strong>

<pre><code>rows before batch execution= 6
Batch executed
rows after batch execution= = 9 
</code></pre>
<p>Source: <a href="http://www.tutorialspoint.com/javaexamples/jdbc_executebatch.htm" rel="nofollow">Execute multiple SQL statements</a></p>');insert into answers values('June',12.0,2.0,1.0,'No',1176.0,'<p>There are two problems in your code. First you use the same <code>Statement</code> object (<code>stmt</code>) to execute the select query, and the insert. In JDBC, executing a statement will close the <code>ResultSet</code> of the previous execute on the same object. </p>
<p>In your code, you loop over the <code>ResultSet</code> and execute an insert for each row. However executing that statement will close the <code>ResultSet</code> and therefor on the next iteration the call to <code>next()</code> will throw an <code>SQLException</code> as the <code>ResultSet</code> is closed.</p>
<p>The solution is to use two <code>Statement</code> objects: one for the select and one for the insert. This will however not always work by default, as you are working in <code>autoCommit</code> (this is the default), and with auto commit, the execution of any statement will commit any previous transactions (which usually also closes the <code>ResultSet</code>, although this may differ between databases and JDBC drivers). You either need to disable auto commit, or create the result set as holdable over commit (unless that already is the default of your JDBC driver).</p>');insert into answers values('June',12.0,3.0,0.0,'No',23900.0,'<p>In the abscence of the schema or the data contained in each table Im going to make the following assumptions:</p>

Therefore, multiplication will be performed using the <code>int</code> type.  Since the mathematical result is 31536000000, and the largest possible <code>int</code> is 2147483648, the result overflows and the result will wrap around.  The result will thus be the <code>int</code> whose value is equivalent to 31536000000 modulo 2<sup>32</sup>, which is 1471228928.  Only then is it converted to a <code>float</code> to be divided into <code>dateDiff</code>.  Appending an <code>L</code> to the end of any of the integer literals will fix it, since now at least one of the multiplications will be performed using <code>long</code>.  But it might be clearer to change <code>365</code> to <code>365.0</code> (or <code>365f</code>).  (Actually, @Chills suggestion to use <code>f</code> on all the constants appears best to me, although its not really necessary.)</p>');insert into answers values('June',17.0,1.0,1.0,'No',3618.0,'<p>Is a question a long time ago and you have probably already found a solution.

<hr>
<p>Skip the heap and just create the HashMap.</p>
<p>After youve created the HashMap, you can iterate through it and put all the elements in an array.</p>
<p>Then you can run a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selection_algorithm" rel="nofollow">selection algorithm</a> such as <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quickselect" rel="nofollow">quickselect</a> on the array to get <code>k</code>-th element, and the first <code>k</code> elements from there (the extension to extract the first <code>k</code> elements via quickselect is fairly trivial, or you can just iterating through again to get them).</p>
<p>Then you sort the <code>k</code> elements, if required.</p>
<p>The running time would be expected <code>O(n)</code> or <code>O(n + k log k)</code> if sorting is required.</p>
<p>The space complexity would be <code>O(n)</code>.</p>');insert into answers values('June',19.0,2.0,0.0,'No',3771.0,'<p>Consider having a Map which maps the number to its count of occurrence. Maintain a separate int which contains the currently largest count of any number and a List containing each of the numbers with /count/ numbers.
This approach will allow you to know the results after a single iteration over all the values. At worst (if all values have 1 occurrence) you use 2x memory (1 entry in both map and list). Even this could be worked around by only starting to add items to the list once a single entry has 2 occurrences.</p>');insert into answers values('June',19.0,3.0,0.0,'No',127.0,'<p>I agree that the heap would be complicating it. I have added the code in C++ below to explain the quickselect method.</p>
<p>Steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>Get frequency of each unique element by using a <code>map</code>.</li>
<li>Perform <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quickselect" rel="nofollow">quickselect</a> to get the largest kth element.</li>
<li>Select the elements in the vector from 0 to k.</li>
</ol>
<p>Code: </p>
<pre><code>#include &lt;cmath&gt;
#include &lt;cstdio&gt;
#include &lt;vector&gt;
#include &lt;iostream&gt;
#include &lt;algorithm&gt;
#include &lt;map&gt;
using namespace std;
map&lt;int,int&gt; m;
void swap(int *a,int *b){
    int temp=*a;
    *a=*b;
    *b=temp;
}
void printelements(vector&lt;int&gt; &amp;temp,int k){
    for(int i=0;i&lt;=k;++i){
        cout&lt;&lt;temp[i]&lt;&lt;endl;
    }
} 
int partition(vector&lt;int&gt; &amp;a, int low,int high){
    int pivot = high-1;
    int i=low-1;
    for(int j=low;j&lt;high-1;j++){
        if(m[a[j]]&gt;=m[a[pivot]]){
            i++;
            swap(&amp;a[i],&amp;a[j]);
        }
    }
    i++;
    swap(&amp;a[i],&amp;a[pivot]);
    return i;
}
void quickselect(vector&lt;int&gt; &amp;temp,int low,int high,int k){
    if(low&gt;high){
        return ;
    }
    int pivot=partition(temp,low,high);
    if(k==pivot){
        printelements(temp,k);
        return;
    }
    else if(k&lt;pivot){
        quickselect(temp,low,pivot,k);
    }
    else{
        quickselect(temp,pivot+1,high,k);
    }
}
void topKelements(int a[],int n,int k){
    if(k&lt;0)return ;
    for(int i=0;i&lt;n;i++){
        if(m.find(a[i])!=m.end()){
            m[a[i]]++;
        }
        else{
            m.insert(pair&lt;int,int&gt;(a[i],1));
        }
    }
    vector&lt;int&gt; temp;
    map&lt;int,int&gt;::iterator it;
    for(it=m.begin();it!=m.end();++it){
        temp.push_back(it-&gt;first);
    }
    k=min(k,(int)temp.size()-1);
    quickselect(temp,0,temp.size(),k);
}
int main() {
    int a[] = {1,2,3,4,1,1,2,3,4,4,4,1};
    int k = 2;
    topKelements(a,12,k-1);
}
</code></pre>
<p>Output:
<code>1 4 2</code></p>');insert into answers values('June',20.0,1.0,0.0,'No',23.0,'<p>I would change the HTML version into something like this:</p>

<p>As mentioned by @greg-449 in the questions comments "The content outline view code does not know anything about multi-page editors and only supports one content outline per editor." </p>
<p>This is true and actually gave me an idea of how to tackle with the problem. The solution that I came up with is related with refreshing the outline view(closing and open it again programmatically) while you navigate among tabs.</p>
<p>So to begin with, I applied the solution in a multipage editor that combines EMF/GMF tabs as well as a StructuredTextEditor for displaying XML.</p>
<h1>What you should already have</h1>
<p>You multipage editor should Override/add the following methods. Note that, this is not a plug &amp; play situation, search on how to create a custom outline page or how call the default outline page based on the editorInput. The reason I am adding this is for understanding. </p>
<hr>
<p><em>(pay attention to the showOutlineView method) It returns false because we want to disable the other views. However, you could offer different outlines per editor if you wish. To do that you will need always return true in the showOutlineView and initialise somehow different the outline page in the getContentOutlinePage() method. Possibly by having different implementation of the page based on the editor requested.</em></p>
<hr>
<pre><code>/**
 * This is how the framework determines which interfaces we implement.
*/
@SuppressWarnings("rawtypes")
@Override
public Object getAdapter(Class key) {
    if (key.equals(IContentOutlinePage.class)) {
        return showOutlineView() ? getContentOutlinePage() : null;
    } else {
        return super.getAdapter(key);
    }
}
/**
 * This accesses a cached version of the content outliner.
 */
public IContentOutlinePage getContentOutlinePage() {
    if (contentOutlinePage == null) {
        //your outlinepage from your editor
        //or create a custom page(s)
    }
    return contentOutlinePage;
}
/**
 * Returns whether the outline view should be presented to the user.
 */
protected boolean showOutlineView() {
    //e.g if StructuredTextEditor xmlEditor;
    //like this we force the editor getAdapter contentOutline part
    //to return false, and therefore the contentoutline will get a value of
    //null that results in "an outline in not available" in the outline view
    if(getActiveEditor() != xmlEditor)) {
        return false;
    }
    return true;
}
</code></pre>
<h1>How to apply the solution</h1>
<p>In order to apply the solution you will need to modify the <strong>pageChange</strong> method as well as introduce a method that refreshes the outline view programatically and call it appropriately.</p>
<pre><code>public void refreshPropertiesView() {
    //get the activePage
    IWorkbenchPage wp =  PlatformUI.getWorkbench().getActiveWorkbenchWindow().getActivePage();
    //Find desired view by its visual ID
    IViewPart myView=wp.findView("org.eclipse.ui.views.ContentOutline");
    //Hide the view :
    wp.hideView(myView);
    try {
      //show the view again     
      PlatformUI.getWorkbench().getActiveWorkbenchWindow().getActivePage().showView("org.eclipse.ui.views.ContentOutline");
    } catch (PartInitException e) {
        // TODO Auto-generated catch block
        e.printStackTrace();
    } 
}
@Override
protected void pageChange(int pageIndex) {
    refreshPropertiesView();
    ....
    ....
    ....
}
</code></pre>
<h1>What the solution does/ How it does it</h1>
<p>The outline view of an editor is initialised while the editor is initialised (e.g when you open a file with the editor). After that point is retrieved and it does not change as it is cached. Now what this workaround do, is to close the outline view programmatically (so as for it to call again our initialisers when it is opened; again programmatically.). When this call is made we can then initialise and display the outline view of our preference.</p>

<p>OpenGL ES has no immediate mode rendering (glBegin, glVertex, glColor). Youll have to load your geometry into VBOs and render that way.</p>
<p>Youll also need to write basic shaders and pass your projection and modelview matrices in via glUniformMatrix.</p>
<p>Immediate mode rendering is pretty much only available on the desktop, iPhones, Androids and Blackberrys use only OpenGL ES and pretty much any game console will use an API very similiar to OpenGL ES.</p>
<p><em>Bottom line:</em> Youll need to ditch the immediate mode rendering and learn to use the ES spec.</p>
<p>These links should help...</p>
<p><a href="http://www.khronos.org/registry/gles/specs/2.0/es_full_spec_2.0.25.pdf" rel="nofollow">http://www.khronos.org/registry/gles/specs/2.0/es_full_spec_2.0.25.pdf</a></p>

<p>===========================================</p>
<p>You will need to have Maven and Firefox installed on your machine in order to run this example.</p>
<p>Once you have retrieved the source, you can run by navigating into the Cucumber-JVM-Parallel directory and issuing the command:</p>
<p>mvn clean install</p>
<p>This will run the example project and start two browser windows concurrently. Each browser window corresponds to a Cucumber feature file in the example. Once the run is complete, a report will have been generated at /target/cucumber-report/index.html.</p>
<p>The rest of this post will go into further detail on the structure of the example project, though it is assumed that you have some prior experience of Cucumber. If not, the Cucumber-JVM readme is a great place to start.</p>
<h2>Feature files</h2>
<p>The first thing you need is your feature files to describe the behaviour you expect. In this example, we have two separate features, though you can also run scenarios within a single feature in parallel.</p>
<p>The way we can do is is by using Cucumber tags, which can be applied either to all scenarios in a feature or to individual scenarios.</p>
<p><img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/svRUE.png" alt="Cucumber tags"></p>
<p>Above, you can see that we have two feature files. These reside in the â??src/test/resourcesâ?? folder. Each feature file is tagged (<code>@autocorrect</code> and <code>@search</code>), and contains a single scenario.</p>
<h2>Glue code</h2>
<p>Now that we have our scenarios, we need to add some glue code to tie each step into our underlying test framework</p>
<p>These are referred to as step definitions, and can be found in â??src/java/cucumber.jvm.parallel/cucumber/stepdefsâ??.</p>
<p><img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/fkfMM.png" alt="code snippet"></p>
<p>In the above snippet, you can see that we use an instance of ShareDriver to communicate directly with a browser window. This is based on one of the cucumber examples for sharing a single browser session between all tests (using dependency injection) to remove the need for starting up a browser instance per test and thus speed up execution. In our case, this results in one browser session per thread. The ShareDriver class can be found in â??/src/test/java/cucumber.jvm.parallel/cucumberâ??.</p>
<h2>Page Objects</h2>
<p>The snippet also shows that we use an instance of â??SearchPageObjectâ??, which is simply a class which represents the Google search page,  found in â??/src/test/java/cucumber.jvm.parallel/pageobjectsâ??.</p>
<p>This is not required, but itâ??s good practice to use the page object pattern for ease of maintainability on a larger project.</p>
<p><img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/13bq7.png" alt="page object"></p>
<p>Above, you can see that the page object contains identifiers for elements on the page as well as methods specific to that page.</p>
<h2>Runners</h2>
<p>The next stage in the process is adding the test runners. We are using JUnit as opposed to the CLI, and this is where we need to start structuring things specifically to handle parallel running of tests.</p>
<p><img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/ndoro.png" alt="runners"></p>
<p>In the above snippet from â??SearchAT.classâ?? you can see that we are specifying the location of the feature files. We are also specifying a tag (<code>@search</code>) which relates to one of our cucumber feature file tags and a html report destination for test results.</p>
<p>What this says is â??run all tests tagged as @search and write results to /search folderâ??.</p>
<p>We then have another class, â??AutoCorrectATâ?? which does the same for all tests tagged â??@autocorrectâ??. Both of these classes can be found under â??/src/test/java/cucumber.jvm.parallel/cucumberâ??.</p>
<p>Adding another thread is simply a case of adding a new runner class with a different tag.</p>
<h2>Parallel Test Runs</h2>
<p>Up to this point, the instructions are identical to creating a relatively simple non-parallel set of Cucumber-JVM tests using WebDriver to interact with a website.</p>
<p>We now need to go to the Maven POM file to see how we are making the tests run in parallel.</p>
<p><img src="http://i.stack.imgur.com/S1fxc.png" alt="POM config"></p>
<p>In the above snippet, you can see that the maven-surefire-plugin is used to run our acceptance tests â?? any classes that end in *AT will be run as a JUnit test class. Thanks to JUnit, making the tests run in parallel is now a simple case of setting the forkCount configuration option. In the example project, this is set to 5, meaning that we can run up to 5 threads (ie, 5 runner classes) at a time.</p>
<p>============================</p>
<p>More details you can get in <a href="http://www.opencredo.com/2013/07/02/running-cucumber-jvm-tests-in-parallel/" rel="nofollow">Running Cucumber-JVM tests in parallel</a>  article</p>
<p>Hope this helps you.</p>');insert into answers values('July',13.0,2.0,0.0,'No',3789.0,'<p>I assume that you use a test task to execute your Cucumber Runners?
If so, you can use this in your build.gradle:</p>
<pre><code>tasks.withType(Test) {
    maxParallelForks = 5
}
task uiTests(type: Test){  includes = [**/*Cucumber*] }
</code></pre>
<p>This uiTests Task assumes that all Runner Classes have Cucumber in their name, if this doesnt suit you, you can just write every Runner class in there.</p>
<p>Now if you provide an own runner for each feature file, the different runners will be executed in parallel</p>

<pre><code>@CucumberOptions{tags = @Feature1}

        sslContext.init(null,
                new TrustManager[]{new X509TrustManager() {
                    public X509Certificate[] getAcceptedIssuers() {
                        return null;
                    }
                    public void checkClientTrusted(
                            X509Certificate[] certs, String authType) {
                    }
                    public void checkServerTrusted(
                            X509Certificate[] certs, String authType) {
                    }
                }}, new SecureRandom());
        SSLConnectionSocketFactory socketFactory = new SSLConnectionSocketFactory(sslContext,SSLConnectionSocketFactory.ALLOW_ALL_HOSTNAME_VERIFIER);
        HttpClient httpClient = HttpClientBuilder.create().setSSLSocketFactory(socketFactory).build();
        return httpClient;
    } catch (Exception e) {
        e.printStackTrace();
        return HttpClientBuilder.create().build();
    }
}

Connected to localhost.

::1         localhost localhost.localdomain localhost6 localhost6.localdomain6
</code></pre>

<pre><code>127.0.0.1   localhost localhost.localdomain localhost4 localhost4.localdomain4
::1         localhost6 localhost6.localdomain6
</code></pre>

But if you are providing an API, and implement your own collection-like class, you can implement <code>Spliterator</code> to adapt your collection to the <code>Stream</code> API. This supports a functional approach, parallel processing, and other features.</p>
<p>For example, I wrote a utility to enumerate IP addresses in a network, specified by CIDR notation. Its not really a collection; that is, it doesnt carry list of all of the addresses in memory at once, only the network number and netmask. But by exposing a <code>Spliterator</code>, it can be easily adapted to a <code>Stream</code>. (Each <code>Spliterator</code> just tracks the current IP address and maximum address in its share of the network.)</p>
<p>Another example from the core Java runtime is <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/api/java/nio/file/Files.html#newDirectoryStream-java.nio.file.Path-" rel="nofollow"><code>DirectoryStream</code> for traversing the file system.</a></p>');insert into answers values('July',22.0,2.0,2.0,'No',14300.0,'<p>Use case example: "Converts iterator to stream"</p>
<pre><code>public static &lt;T&gt; Stream&lt;T&gt; iteratorToFiniteStream(final Iterator&lt;T&gt; iterator) {
   final Iterable&lt;T&gt; iterable = () -&gt; iterator;
  return StreamSupport.stream(iterable.spliterator(), false);
}
</code></pre>');insert into answers values('July',22.0,3.0,1.0,'No',173.0,'<p><code>Spliterator</code> is an extension of the timeless <code>Iterator</code> class that allows for splitting of a stream of objects to iterate over (<code>Stream</code> works by collecting the operations before iterating).</p>
<p>I cannot think of any times when the average developer would have to work with <code>Spliterator</code>. The <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/api/java/util/Collection.html" rel="nofollow"><code>Collection</code></a> and <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/api/java/util/Collections.html" rel="nofollow"><code>Collections</code></a> APIs are incredibly rich in Java 8, and in most cases youd be better off using a vanilla <code>Collection</code> subclass instead of building your own <code>Stream</code> interface.</p>
<p>An example of when you might want to use <code>Spliterator</code> might be a library for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graph_theory" rel="nofollow">graphs</a> using a linked data structure over which the standard <code>Spliterator</code>/<code>stream()</code> is undefined.</p>');insert into answers values('July',23.0,1.0,0.0,'No',3844.0,'<p>The problem is it takes the xml as string. if you can define the content type it should work.

<pre><code>public void update(GameContainer container, int delta)
{
    playerUpdate(delta);
    player.rect.setLocation(playX, playY);
    enemy.rect.setLocation(enemyX, enemyY); // update the hitboxes to the new positions
    if (player.rect.intersects(enemy.rect))
    {
        System.out.println("INTERSECT!");
    }
}
public void playerUpdate(int delta)
{
    if (playerForward == true)
    {
       playX -= delta * 0.4f;
       if (playX &lt;= 140) 
       {
             playX = 140;
             playerForward = false;
             playerBackward = true;
       }
    }
    if (playerBackward == true) 
    {
         playX += delta * 0.4f;
         if (playX &gt;= 700) 
         {
             playX = 700;
             playerBackward = false;
             delay = 1250;
         }
    }
}
public void keyReleased(int key, char c) 
{
   if (key == Input.KEY_ENTER)
   {
      playerForward = true;
   }
}
</code></pre>
<p>Furthermore, as you seem to be new to game development in Java, some tips for you:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Format your code properly</strong> </li>
</ul>
<p>Always place full {...} after if, else, switch, while, for, etc.; proper line indentation, .</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Think OO (Object-Oriented)</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>This one is pretty important. Your enemy and player class should both extend some kind of entity class because they both will pretty much want to obtain similar behavior (avoid code duplication!). Sum up similar behavior to a super class, simplify the behavior to be controlled with a few adjustable parameters and so on.</p>
<p>For example, you store the positions of your enemy and player as a static integer in your main class. This is not OO. Move the positions to the entity class where you can implement it in whatever manner you wish.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Dont just throw an exception for no reason</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>Your update(...) method throws a SlickException even though its never needed.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Be careful about encapsulation</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>This is something a lot of beginners do: Just grab some parameters, put them in a class as private (or maybe even public) and generate getters- and setters for them. This is <strong>not</strong> encapsulation. This is almost as bad as making them public in the first place. </p>
<p>But why dont we just make everything public?</p>
<p>We dont want anyone (or even ourselves) to rely on some parameters that just happen to be there because of some very specific implementation of something we might want to change later. Dont just put all possible values out there to be changed, the sense of encapsulation is to be independent from what kind of implementation we end up using and to protect the usability of our code by guarding what can be set/changed.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Performance does matter</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>This is one of the aspects you should watch out for, for any kind of software, but you can often most drastically see the consequences in games. Performance is important! And by that, I dont mean that you have to watch out for every single detail, but just keep an overview in mind on how to improve and fasten up your code, especially with frequently called methods such as update(..) and render(..) in Slick2D.</p>
<p><strong>Update</strong></p>
<p>As a solution to another problem discussed in the comments:</p>
<pre><code>public class Enemy {
    private int startX, startY, width, height;
    public Shape rect = new Rectangle(startX, startY, width, height);
    // plus getters and setters
}
</code></pre>
<p>width and height can only be 0 as they are never assigned an integers have the value 0 per default, so the enemy rectangle hitbox does have 0 width and will never trigger. </p>
<p>Try something like:</p>
<pre><code> public class Enemy {
    private int startX, startY, width = 50, height = 70;
    public Shape rect = new Rectangle(startX, startY, width, height);
    // plus getters and setters
 }
</code></pre>
<p>This should work, but you should probably move all these attributes to the enemy class and put them in the constructor.</p>');insert into answers values('July',27.0,1.0,1.0,'Yes',119.0,'<p>Building on what is mentioned in the comments, the simplest solution would be:</p>

<p>Full duplex is fairly simple to do with NIO:</p>
<ol>
<li>Create a <code>Channel</code> for your <code>Socket</code> in non-blocking mode</li>
<li>Add read to the interest OPs</li>
<li>Sleep with a <code>Selector</code>s <code>select()</code> method</li>
<li>Read any readable bytes, write any writable bytes</li>
<li>If writing is done, remove write from interest OPs</li>
<li>GOTO 3.</li>
<li>If you need to write, add bytes to a buffer, add write to interest OPs and wake up selector. (slightly simplified, but Im sure you can find your way around the Javadoc)</li>
</ol>
<p>This way you will be completely loading the outgoing buffer every time there is space and reading from the incoming one at the same time (well, single thread, but you dont have to finish writing to start reading etc).</p>');insert into answers values('July',30.0,3.0,0.0,'No',48.0,'<p>I had run into the same question and decided to answer it myself. <p>  </p>
<p>If you use this as-is, everytime you scroll up in that view, the SwipeRefreshLayout fires and updates, making your app unable to scroll up in a list.</p>
<p>The trick here is to wire the OnScrollListener from the ListView manually. You just check if the first row being shown matches the first top-most position, and then enable the SwipeRefreshLayout. Otherwise, disable it.</p>
<pre><code>guidesList.setOnScrollListener(new AbsListView.OnScrollListener() {  
@Override
public void onScrollStateChanged(AbsListView view, int scrollState) {
}
  @Override
  public void onScroll(AbsListView view, int firstVisibleItem,
  int visibleItemCount, int totalItemCount) {
 int topRowVerticalPosition = 
    (guidesList == null || guidesList.getChildCount() == 0) ? 
      0 : guidesList.getChildAt(0).getTop();
  swipeContainer.setEnabled(firstVisibleItem == 0 &amp;&amp;
  topRowVerticalPosition &gt;= 0);
  }
 });
</code></pre>
<p>With this little snippet now it works perfectly.</p>
<p>Happy coding!</p>

<p>The documentation for SwipeRefreshLayout says that the ListView should be the only child, but it is okay if it has more than one child as long as the ListView is first.  This means, for instance, that SwipeRefreshLayout will work fine if you are using an adapter with a view for "empty".  For example:</p>

</code></pre>

</code></pre>

    &lt;SwipeRefreshLayout&gt;    )
         &lt;ListView/&gt;         fragment
         &lt;TextView/&gt;        /

&lt;/FrameLayout&gt;

</code></pre>

<pre><code>void update(Map&lt;String, Object&gt; json, String path, Object newValue);
</code></pre>
<p>Ive quickly done a gist of a dirty implementation for simple specific paths (no support for conditions and wildcards) that can traverse json tree, E.g. $.store.name, $.store.books[0].isbn. Here it is: <a href="https://gist.github.com/vlad-at-yteq/4c42fe4a6874317b81b9#file-mutablejson-java" rel="nofollow">MutableJson.java</a>. It definitely needs improvement, but can give a good start.</p>
<p>Usage example:</p>
<pre><code>import java.util.*;
public class MutableJson {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        MutableJson json = new MutableJson(
                new HashMap&lt;String, Object&gt;() {{
                    put("store", new HashMap&lt;String, Object&gt;() {{
                        put("name", "Some Store");
                        put("books", Arrays.asList(
                                new HashMap&lt;String, Object&gt;() {{
                                    put("isbn", "111");
                                }},
                                new HashMap&lt;String, Object&gt;() {{
                                    put("isbn", "222");
                                }}
                        ));
                    }});
                }}
        );
        System.out.println("Before:	" + json.map());
        json.update("$.store.name", "Book Store");
        json.update("$.store.books[0].isbn", "444");
        json.update("$.store.books[1].isbn", "555");
        System.out.println("After:	" + json.map());
    }
    private final Map&lt;String, Object&gt; json;
    public MutableJson(Map&lt;String, Object&gt; json) {
        this.json = json;
    }
    public Map&lt;String, Object&gt; map() {
        return json;
    }
    public void update(String path, Object newValue) {
        updateJson(this.json, Path.parse(path), newValue);
    }
    private void updateJson(Map&lt;String, Object&gt; data, Iterator&lt;Token&gt; path, Object newValue) {
        Token token = path.next();
        for (Map.Entry&lt;String, Object&gt; entry : data.entrySet()) {
            if (!token.accept(entry.getKey(), entry.getValue())) {
                continue;
            }
            if (path.hasNext()) {
                Object value = token.value(entry.getValue());
                if (value instanceof Map) {
                    updateJson((Map&lt;String, Object&gt;) value, path, newValue);
                }
            } else {
                token.update(entry, newValue);
            }
        }
    }
}
class Path {
    public static Iterator&lt;Token&gt; parse(String path) {
        if (path.isEmpty()) {
            return Collections.&lt;Token&gt;emptyList().iterator();
        }
        if (path.startsWith("$.")) {
            path = path.substring(2);
        }
        List&lt;Token&gt; tokens = new ArrayList&lt;&gt;();
        for (String part : path.split("\.")) {
            if (part.matches("\w+\[\d+\]")) {
                String fieldName = part.substring(0, part.indexOf([));
                int index = Integer.parseInt(part.substring(part.indexOf([)+1, part.indexOf(])));
                tokens.add(new ArrayToken(fieldName, index));
            } else {
                tokens.add(new FieldToken(part));
            }
        };
        return tokens.iterator();
    }
}
abstract class Token {
    protected final String fieldName;
    Token(String fieldName) {
        this.fieldName = fieldName;
    }
    public abstract Object value(Object value);
    public abstract boolean accept(String key, Object value);
    public abstract void update(Map.Entry&lt;String, Object&gt; entry, Object newValue);
}
class FieldToken extends Token {
    FieldToken(String fieldName) {
        super(fieldName);
    }
    @Override
    public Object value(Object value) {
        return value;
    }
    @Override
    public boolean accept(String key, Object value) {
        return fieldName.equals(key);
    }
    @Override
    public void update(Map.Entry&lt;String, Object&gt; entry, Object newValue) {
        entry.setValue(newValue);
    }
}
class ArrayToken extends Token {
    private final int index;
    ArrayToken(String fieldName, int index) {
        super(fieldName);
        this.index = index;
    }
    @Override
    public Object value(Object value) {
        return ((List) value).get(index);
    }
    @Override
    public boolean accept(String key, Object value) {
        return fieldName.equals(key) &amp;&amp; value instanceof List &amp;&amp; ((List) value).size() &gt; index;
    }
    @Override
    public void update(Map.Entry&lt;String, Object&gt; entry, Object newValue) {
        List list = (List) entry.getValue();
        list.set(index, newValue);
    }
}
</code></pre>
<p>A JSON string can be easily parsed into a Map using Jackson:</p>
<pre><code>Map&lt;String,Object&gt; userData = new ObjectMapper().readValue("{ "store": ... }", Map.class);
</code></pre>');insert into answers values('August',20.0,2.0,0.0,'No',1100.0,'<p>So in order to change a value within a JSon string, there are two steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>Parse the JSon</li>
<li>Modify the appropriate field</li>
</ol>
<p>You are trying to optimize step 2, but understand that you are not going to be able to avoid step 1. Looking at the Json-path source code (which, really, is just a wrapper around <a href="https://github.com/FasterXML/jackson" rel="nofollow">Jackson</a>), note that it does do a full parse of the Json string before being able to spit out the read value. It does this parse every time you call <code>read()</code>, e.g. it is not cached.</p>
<p>I think this task is specific enough that youre going to have to write it yourself. Here is what I would do:</p>
<ol>
<li>Create an object that represents the data in the parsed Json string.
<ul>
<li>Make sure this object has, as part of its fields, the Json <code>String</code> pieces that you do not expect to change often.</li>
</ul></li>
<li>Create a custom Deserializer in the Json framework of your choice that will populate the fields correctly.</li>
<li>Create a custom Serializer that uses the cached <code>String</code> pieces, plus the data that you expect to change</li>
</ol>
<p>I think the exact scope of your problem is unusual enough that it is unlikely a library already exists for this. When a program receives a Json <code>String</code>, most of the time what it wants is the fully deserialized object - it is unusual that it needs to FORWARD this object on to somewhere else.</p>');insert into answers values('August',20.0,3.0,0.0,'No',4576.0,'<p><em>Just answering for folks landing on this page in future for reference.</em></p>

<blockquote>
  <p>JSON Patch is a format for describing changes to a JSON document. It can be used to avoid sending a whole document when only a part has changed. When used in combination with the HTTP PATCH method it allows partial updates for HTTP APIs in a standards compliant way.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>You can specify the operation that needs to be performed (replace, add....), json path at which it has to be performed, and the value which should be used.</p>

<pre><code> [
     { "op": "test", "path": "/a/b/c", "value": "foo" },
     { "op": "remove", "path": "/a/b/c" },
     { "op": "add", "path": "/a/b/c", "value": [ "foo", "bar" ] },

     { "op": "copy", "from": "/a/b/d", "path": "/a/b/e" }
   ]
</code></pre>

<h1>Background: Eclipse <em>access restrictions</em></h1>
<p>Eclipse has a mechanism called <em>access restrictions</em> to prevent you from accidentally using classes which Eclipse thinks are not part of the public API. Usually, Eclipse is right about that, in both senses: We usually do not want to use something which is not part of the public API. And Eclipse is usually right about what is and what isnt part of the public API.</p>
<h1>Problem</h1>
<p>Now, there can be situations, where you want to use non-public API. And there can be situations, where Eclipse is not really right (thats what happened to me, I just wanted to use <code>javax.smartcardio</code>). In that case, we get this error in Eclipse.</p>
<h1>Solution</h1>
<p>The solution is to change the access restrictions. Go to the properties of your Java project, i.e. by selecting "Properties" from the context menu of the project in the "Package Explorer". There, go to "Java Build Path", tab "Libraries". There, select "Access rules", "Edit..." and "Add..." a "Resolution: Accessible" with a corresponding rule pattern. For me that was "<code>javax/smartcardio/**</code>", for you it might instead by "<code>com/apple/eawt/**</code>".</p>');insert into answers values('August',24.0,4.0,0.0,'No',2592.0,'<p>I had this problem because the project facet associated with my project was the wrong java version.</p>

<pre><code>import org.easymock.EasyMock;

import org.junit.Test;
import org.powermock.reflect.Whitebox;
public class TestA {
    private A a = new A();
    private B b = EasyMock.createMock(B.class);
    @Before
    public void init() {
        Whitebox.setInternalState(a, "b", b);
    }
    @Test
    public void testInit() {
        EasyMock.reset(b);
        //define mock behavior here
        EasyMock.replay(b);
        a.init();
        //assert and verify
        EasyMock.verify(b);
    }

   &lt;fx:deploy width="${javafx.run.width}" height="${javafx.run.height}" 
             nativeBundles="all"
             outdir="${basedir}/${dist.dir}" outfile="${application.title}"&gt;
      &lt;fx:application name="${application.title}" mainClass="${javafx.main.class}"/&gt;
      &lt;fx:resources&gt;
          &lt;fx:fileset dir="${basedir}/${dist.dir}" includes="*.jar"/&gt;
          &lt;!--below is the magic bit that copies all the dependency jar files to the native package output--&gt;
          &lt;fx:fileset dir="${basedir}/${dist.dir}" includes="lib/*.jar"/&gt;
      &lt;/fx:resources&gt;
      &lt;fx:info title="MyApp" vendor="MyVendor"/&gt;
  &lt;/fx:deploy&gt;          
&lt;/target&gt;
</code></pre>

A timeline creates a thread that repeats a set amount of times or infinitely until you terminate it.<br>
Here is how you would at it:</p>
<p><strong>MainControl:</strong></p>
<pre><code>package application;
import java.net.URL;
import java.util.ResourceBundle;
import javafx.animation.KeyFrame;
import javafx.animation.Timeline;
import javafx.animation.TimelineBuilder;
import javafx.event.ActionEvent;
import javafx.event.EventHandler;
import javafx.fxml.Initializable;
import javafx.util.Duration;
@SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
public class MainControl implements Initializable{
    public void initialize(URL arg0, ResourceBundle arg1) {
    Timeline tick = TimelineBuilder.create()//creates a new Timeline
     .keyFrames(
       new KeyFrame(
            new Duration(10),//This is how often it updates in milliseconds
            new EventHandler&lt;ActionEvent&gt;() {
                  public void handle(ActionEvent t) {
                       //You put what you want to update here
                  }
            }
        )
     )
    .cycleCount(Timeline.INDEFINITE)
    .build();
tick.play();//Starts the timeline
    }

<p>Your <code>count</code> is going to always start one too high, since the last part of the <code>for</code> loop is going to be to increment it again. </p>
<p>You need the <code>while</code> loop to run when <code>count</code> is 0 to check the last bit.</p>
<p>The rest looks like it should be good, but I dont understand what the statements mean with <code>newNum</code>.</p>
<p>An easier version of your algorithm is to use bitwise operators -- instead of having to divide by powers of two explicitly with <code>Math.pow</code>, you can use bitwise operators to test if bits are on or off, and then print out 1s and 0s accordingly. For example:</p>
<pre><code>public static void toBinary(int n) {
   int mask = 1, nn = n;
   while(nn != 0) {
      mask &lt;&lt; 1;
      nn /= 2;
   }
   mask &gt;&gt;= 1;
   while(mask != 0) {
      System.out.print( (mask &amp; n) ? "1" : "0" );
      mask &gt;&gt;= 1;
   }
}
</code></pre>
<p>EDIT: Also, your <code>userNum = userNum</code> is redundant in the <code>for</code> loop. Just use a null statement (<code>;</code>) in the assignment part of the loop instead. So:</p>
<p><code>for(; (Math.pow(2, count) &lt;= userNum); count++) {</code></p>');insert into answers values('September',17.0,1.0,0.0,'No',1.0,'<p>If you use a javaws from a java 1.7 u25 or earlier, your application client will work.</p>

So, if you started your program and then typed the whole <code>.in</code> file into the console window, it would work.</p>
<p>But you dont want to have to type the file every time, instead you can <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redirection_%28computing%29" rel="nofollow">redirect</a> the input to read from the <code>.in</code> file instead of the keyboard. As far as I can see, there is no option to do that in Eclipse, but you can do it from the command line by appending <code>&lt;</code> followed by the file name to the normal command to start your program. The whole command could look something like:</p>
<pre><code>java -jar A.jar &lt; A-small.in
</code></pre>
<p>Another option is to take the name of the input file as an argument of your program (thats what the Eclipse option you used is for). Those arguments are accessible from the <code>args</code> parameter of your <code>main</code> method. To do it this way, you actually have to tell to <code>Scanner</code> to use that file:</p>
<pre><code>Scanner in = new Scanner(new File(args[0]));
</code></pre>
<p>Yet another option would be to hard-code the file name:</p>
<pre><code>Scanner in = new Scanner(new File("A-small.in"));
</code></pre>
<p>Doing it this way would be considered a bad practice in any kind of production code, but it might be okay for a programming contest.</p>');insert into answers values('September',22.0,1.0,0.0,'No',200.0,'<ul>
<li>because Spinner uses TextField as an editor, users can insert any String into spinner</li>
<li>only after user hits the return key then Spinners model (SpinnerValueFactory implementation) validates users input</li>
</ul>
<p>so you have to add validation to Spinners editor by code:</p>
<pre class="lang-java prettyprint-override"><code>// imports omitted
public class MainApp extends Application {
protected static final String INITAL_VALUE = "0";
public static void main(String[] args) {
    Application.launch(args);
}
@Override
public void start(Stage stage) {
    final Spinner spinner = new Spinner();
    spinner.setValueFactory(new SpinnerValueFactory.IntegerSpinnerValueFactory(0, 10000,
            Integer.parseInt(INITAL_VALUE)));
    spinner.setEditable(true);
    EventHandler&lt;KeyEvent&gt; enterKeyEventHandler;
    enterKeyEventHandler = new EventHandler&lt;KeyEvent&gt;() {
        @Override
        public void handle(KeyEvent event) {
            // handle users "enter key event"
            if (event.getCode() == KeyCode.ENTER) {
                try {
    // yes, using exception for control is a bad solution ;-)
            Integer.parseInt(spinner.getEditor().textProperty().get());
                }
                catch (NumberFormatException e) {
                    // show message to user: "only numbers allowed"
                    // reset editor to INITAL_VALUE
                    spinner.getEditor().textProperty().set(INITAL_VALUE);
                }
            }
        }
    };
    // note: use KeyEvent.KEY_PRESSED, because KeyEvent.KEY_TYPED is to late, spinners
    // SpinnerValueFactory reached new value before key released an SpinnerValueFactory will
    // throw an exception
    spinner.getEditor().addEventHandler(KeyEvent.KEY_PRESSED, enterKeyEventHandler);
    GridPane grid = new GridPane();
    grid.setHgap(10);
    grid.setVgap(10);
    grid.setPadding(new Insets(10));
    int row = 0;
    grid.add(new Label("Spinner:"), 0, row);
    grid.add(spinner, 1, row);
    Scene scene = new Scene(grid, 350, 300);
    stage.setTitle("Hello Spinner");
    stage.setScene(scene);
    stage.show();
}
}
</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>try with not numbers: code will replace spinners editor content with INITIAL_VALUE</li>
<li>try with numbers out of border, spinners model will reset spinners editor to valid value</li>
</ul>');insert into answers values('September',22.0,2.0,0.0,'No',1.0,'<p>Not entirely certain about the requirement - assuming that you want to prevent the input of characters that wouldnt parse to valid Number.</p>
<p>If so, usage of a TextFormatter in the Spinners editor comes to the rescue: with it, youll monitor any change of text and either accept or reject it. The decision is encapsulated inside the formatters filter. A very simple version (theres definitely more to do, see Swings DefaultFormatter)</p>

Thats why the inconsistency. Instead of execute, use submit method to submit tasks to executor as it returns you a Future instance, which can be used to wait for the task to complete.</p>
<p>Checkout the <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/util/concurrent/Future.html" rel="nofollow">Futures</a> javadoc</p>
<pre><code>public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException, ExecutionException {
    int[] arr1 = new int[] { 10 };
    int[] arr2 = new int[] { 400 };
    int[] arr3 = new int[] { 20 };
    int[] arr4 = new int[] { 40 };
    List&lt;int[]&gt; list = new ArrayList&lt;int[]&gt;();
    list.add(arr1);
    list.add(arr2);
    list.add(arr3);
    list.add(arr4);
    List&lt;Integer&gt; result = new ArrayList&lt;Integer&gt;();
    List&lt;Future&lt;?&gt;&gt; futures = new ArrayList&lt;Future&lt;?&gt;&gt;();
    ExecutorService executorService = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(3);
    for (int[] array : list) {
        futures.add(executorService.submit(new MyRunnable(result, array)));
    }
    executorService.shutdown();
    for (Future&lt;?&gt; future : futures) {
        future.get();
    }
    System.out.println(result);
}
</code></pre>');insert into answers values('September',25.0,4.0,0.0,'No',561.0,'<p>It seems that sometimes ExecutorService shutdowns until some or your MyRunnable.run are finished. Generally speaking, ExecutorService.execute+Runnable allow you to do "some work" in parallel when you arent interested in the result. If you need to wait until all results are calculated, use ExecutorService.invokeAll+Callable. See for example: </p>
<p><a href="http://tutorials.jenkov.com/java-util-concurrent/executorservice.html" rel="nofollow">http://tutorials.jenkov.com/java-util-concurrent/executorservice.html</a></p>
<p>And, finally, store the result of calculation in a thread safe collection:</p>
<pre><code>public static class MyCallable implements Callable&lt;Boolean&gt; {
    private Set&lt;Integer&gt; numbers;
    private int[] arrayToFind;
    public MyCallable(Set&lt;Integer&gt; numbers, int[] arrayToFind) {
        this.numbers = numbers;
        this.arrayToFind = arrayToFind;
    }
    private boolean isNumber(int n) {
        return n % 10 == 0;
    }
    @Override
    public Boolean call() {
        for (int i = 0; i &lt; arrayToFind.length; i++) {
            if (isNumber(arrayToFind[i]))
                numbers.add(arrayToFind[i]);
        }
        return true;
    }
}
public static void main(String... args) throws InterruptedException{
    int[] arr1 = new int[] {10};
    int[] arr2 = new int[] {400};
    int[] arr3 = new int[] {20};
    int[] arr4 = new int[] {40};
    List&lt;int[]&gt; list = new ArrayList&lt;&gt;();
    list.add(arr1);
    list.add(arr2);
    list.add(arr3);
    list.add(arr4);
    Set&lt;Integer&gt; result = Collections.newSetFromMap(new ConcurrentHashMap&lt;Integer, Boolean&gt;());
    List&lt;MyCallable&gt; myCallables = new ArrayList&lt;&gt;();
    for (int[] array : list) {
        myCallables.add(new MyCallable(result, array));
    }
    ExecutorService executorService = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(3);
    executorService.invokeAll(myCallables);
    executorService.shutdown();
    System.out.println(result);
}

<p>What I found that if you do not set the context loader by @ContextConfiguration annotation on your test class, the default context loader will be used, which derived from AbstractGenericContextLoader. I had a look at its source and turned out it registers all the bean post processors which are responsible for reading annotations such @Autowired. In other words, annotation config is enabled by default.  </p>
<p>So the main problem is that there are two configurations which are in conflict: in the java config we said that autowiring is not needed, while the autowired annotation tells the opposite. The real question is how to disable the annotation processing in order to eliminate the undesired configuration.  </p>
<p>As far as I know there is no such spring implementation of ContextLoader which would not be derived from AbstractGenericContextLoader so I guess the only we can do is to write our own. It would be something like this:</p>
<pre><code>public static class SimpleContextLoader implements ContextLoader {
    @Override
    public String[] processLocations(Class&lt;?&gt; type, String... locations) {
        return strings;
    }
    @Override
    public ApplicationContext loadContext(String... locations) throws Exception {
        // in case of xml configuration
        return new ClassPathXmlApplicationContext(strings);
        // in case of java configuration (but its name is quite misleading)
        // return new AnnotationConfigApplicationContext(TestConfig.class);
    }
}
</code></pre>
<p>Of course it would be worth to spend more time to find out how to implement ContextLoader properly.</p>
<p>Cheers,<br>
Robert</p>');insert into answers values('September',27.0,3.0,0.0,'No',11.0,'<p>There are so many ways of doing this, Im pretty sure that this answer will be incomplete, but here are a few options...</p>
<p>As <em>currently</em> seems to be recommended practice, use constructor injection for your services rather than autowiring the fields directly. This makes testing like this <em>so</em> much easier.</p>
<pre><code>public class SomeTest {
    @Mock
    private ThirdPartyService mockedBean;
    @Before
    public void init() {
        initMocks(this);
    }
    @Test
    public void test() {
        BeanUnderTest bean = new BeanUnderTest(mockedBean);
        // ...
    }
}
public class BeanUnderTest{
    private ThirdPartyService service;
    @Autowired
    public BeanUnderTest(ThirdPartyService ThirdPartyService) {
        this.thirdPartyService = thirdPartyService;
    }
}
</code></pre>
<p>By doing that, you can also mix up autowired and mocked services by autowiring into the test itself and then constructing the beans under test with the most useful mix of autowired and mocked beans.</p>
<p>A reasonable alternative is to use Spring profiles to define stub services. This is particularly useful when wish to use the same stubbed features in multiple tests:</p>
<pre><code>@Service
@Primary
@Profile("test")
public class MyServiceStub implements MyService {
    // ...
}
@RunWith(SpringJUnit4ClassRunner.class)
@ContextConfiguration(classes = SomeTest.Beans.class) 
@ActiveProfiles({"test"})
public class SomeTest {
    // ...
}
</code></pre>
<p>By using the <code>@Primary</code> annotation, it ensures that this stub bean will be used instead of any other bean implementing the <code>MyService</code> interface. I tend to use this approach for things like email services, where by changing profile, Im able to switch between a real mail server and Wiser.</p>');insert into answers values('September',27.0,4.0,0.0,'No',3629.0,'<p>You could add the mocked service manually to the spring application context via org.springframework.beans.factory.config.SingletonBeanRegistry#registerSingleton.     }

<p>A workaround could be this one:</p>
<pre><code>System.out.println("Enter id");
id1 = in.nextInt();
in.nextLine();   // skip the newline character
System.out.println("Enter name");
name1 = in.nextLine();
</code></pre>
<p>Another way would be to always use <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/util/Scanner.html#nextLine()" rel="nofollow"><code>nextLine</code></a> wrapped into a <code>Integer.parseInt</code>:</p>
<pre><code>int id1;
try {
    System.out.println("Enter id");
    id1 = Integer.parseInt(input.nextLine());
} catch (NumberFormatException e) {
    e.printStackTrace();
}
System.out.println("Enter name");
name1 = in.nextLine();
</code></pre>
<h3>Why not just <code>Scanner.next()</code> ?</h3>
<p>I would not use <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/java/util/Scanner.html#nextInt()" rel="nofollow"><code>Scanner.next()</code></a> because this will read only the next token and not the full line. For example the following code:</p>
<pre><code>System.out("Enter name: ");
String name = in.next();
System.out(name);
</code></pre>
<p>will produce:</p>
<pre><code>Enter name: Mad Scientist
Mad
</code></pre>
<p>It will not process <em>Scientist</em> because <em>Mad</em> is already a completed token per se.
So maybe this is the expected behavior for your application, but it has a different semantic from the code you posted in the question.</p>');insert into answers values('October',6.0,2.0,3.0,'No',906.0,'<p>This is your updated working code.   </p>

<ol>
<li>On First Client Time connection client sends a credential pair (username and password)</li>
<li>Server accept this and authenticate, if authenticated it create a hashcode out of it (username &amp; password) and add into list of active session. and return the hashed session to client</li>
<li>On 2nd request or later on client sends the hashed session and server check that session in active list of session.</li>
</ol>
<p>Client Code:</p>
<pre><code>Class Client
{
    private String uname;
    private String password;
    private String session;
    public String[2] message;
    //getter setter
}
//Inside Main Class
int sendInfo(String mesg)
{
    Client c=getClient(); //this function gives your Client Object with either session and username password etc preset,
    if(c.getSession()!==null || !c.getSession()!="")
    {
        c.message[0]=c.getSession(); //first String contains your session 
        c.message[1]=mesg;          //next string contains your message
    }
    else
    {
        c.message[0]=c.getUsername+"|"+c.getPassword(); //first String contains your session 
        c.message[1]=mesg;          //next string contains your message
    }
    sendMessageToServer(c.message);
}
</code></pre>

            //it contains session. Check in activeSesion list

        //It cotains username &amp; password separeted by |. Call Authenticate

        }

            //if the uname and pass is valid
            this.addActiveSession(generateSession(username,password))

In those properties you can specify defaults for the getLine() methods (getLine(), getClip(), getSourceDataLine() and getTargetDataLine()). If you call one  of these methods, Java does the following (<a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/api/javax/sound/sampled/AudioSystem.html" rel="nofollow">AudioSystem description</a>):</p>
<p>The system property javax.sound.sampled.Clip is set to</p>
<p>javax.sound.sampled.Clip = great.Mixer#great.clip.Clap</p>
<p>The Mixer class is called <em>great.Mixer</em> and the Clip is called <em>great.clip.Clap</em></p>
<p>When you request a Clip, Java checks the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>If the Mixer <em>great.Mixer</em> is found and contains the Clip <em>great.clip.Clap</em>, return this Clip</li>
<li>If the Mixer <em>great.Mixer</em> is found, but does not contain the Clip <em>great.clip.Clap</em>, return the first Clip specified in the Mixer</li>
<li>If the Mixer <em>great.Mixer</em> does not contain any Clips or if it isnt found, return the first instance of <em>great.clip.Clap</em> in any Mixer</li>
<li>If no Mixer contains <em>great.clip.Clap</em>, return the first Clip of the first Mixer found</li>
<li>If no Clip is specified in any Mixer, throw an <strong>IllegalArgumentException</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>What that means is that if you are getting an IllegalArgumentException, no Clips are installed in any Mixers.</p>
<p>With</p>
<pre><code>DataLine.Info info = new DataLine.Info(Clip.class, format);
</code></pre>
<p>you are defining a new Clip. Which means your next Call to a getLine() method will return this object instead of giving you an error.</p>');insert into answers values('October',12.0,1.0,1.0,'Yes',268.0,'<p>Im not entirely sure I understand your question. They wont look at the class file to see if it has changed.</p>
<p>(There is a good reason for this.  Basically, the identity of an object type in Java is equivalent to a tuple consisting of the classes fully qualified name, and its class loader.  This means that the JVM cannot (and will not) allow a classloader to "define" two classes with the same name.  If you try to make this happen, I think that the <code>defineClass</code> method will just give you back the <code>Class</code> object for the previously loaded class.)</p>
<p>So ...</p>
<p>In order to achieve what you are trying to achieve, you need to create a new ClassLoader <em>each time</em> you want to load a new version of a class.</p>');insert into answers values('October',22.0,1.0,1.0,'Yes',113.0,'<p>I found your question while looking for an answer. If totalSize is your entity content length, then you can base your progress on that:</p>
<pre><code>class ProgressiveOutputStream extends ProxyOutputStream {
                    long totalSent;
                    long totalSize;
                    public ProgressiveOutputStream(OutputStream proxy, long total) {
                        super(proxy);
                        totalSent = 0;
                        totalSize = total;
                    }
                    public void write(byte[] bts, int st, int end) throws IOException {
                        totalSent += end;
                        publishProgress((int) ((totalSent / (float) totalSize) * 100));
                        out.write(bts, st, end);
                    }
                }
                yourEntity.writeTo(new ProgressiveOutputStream(outstream, yourEntity.getContentLength()));
</code></pre>
<p>You update your progressbar in OnProgressUpdate of your asyncTask (pb is the progressBar):</p>
<pre><code>@Override
    protected void onProgressUpdate(Integer... values) {
        super.onProgressUpdate(values);
        pb.setProgress(values[0]);
    }
</code></pre>');insert into answers values('October',29.0,1.0,1.0,'Yes',92.0,'<p>If you want to store the width/height in the file, that method could work with a little tweaking. An input file could look like this:</p>
<pre><code>12
9
############
#.#........#
#.#.######.#
#.#....#...#
#.###.*#.#.#
#...####.#.#
#.#.#..#.#.#
#.#.#.##.#.#
#o#......#.#

this.height = Integer.parseInt(file.next());
</code></pre>
<p>would be</p>
<pre><code>this.width = Integer.parseInt(file.nextLine());
this.height = Integer.parseInt(file.nextLine());
</code></pre>
<p>A much better way to get the width and height would be to determine them from the files actual dimensions (Note: including the dimensions at the top of the input file for this method would mess things up). Instead of passing in a Scanner to <code>Maze</code>s constructor, pass in the File itself. <p>If you need to aggregate them (which it sounds like you do), that would eventually need to happen in one actor. This means that your 1 million answers will all queue up on the single actor and it will become a hotspot.</p>
<p>If you can tolerate slightly slower reads, another possibility is to have multiple counter actors, which are themselves part of a router (lets say RoundRobin for now). This divides up the counting to multiple actors, but now to get the real total count you would have to ask all of the actors and aggregate them at read time. This strategy could be beneficial if you want to record a lot of "answers", but only read them occasionally when latency may be less important.</p>');insert into answers values('November',2.0,1.0,3.0,'Yes',348.0,'<p>I think you have interchanged the interceptors:</p>

<pre><code>siginfo:si_signo=SIGSEGV: si_errno=0, si_code=1 (SEGV_MAPERR), si_addr=0x0000000000000000
</code></pre>
<p>If you look at the first part, SIGSEGV, that means you have a segmentation fault somewhere in your system. SEGV_MAPERR is the specific error, which means that OpenJDK was trying to map memory to an object and failed. This couldve been caused by not enough memory, a bad pagefile/virtual memory, bad address space, or even a bad library. Why it worked on another machine could be anything. Core dumps are really useful, so if you can run</p>
<pre><code>ulimit -c unlimited
</code></pre>
<p>that will help give you something to look at. Was this in a VM or on a physical machine? Ive seen random sigsegv in my Ubuntu VMs if they dont have enough memory allocated for various Java tasks. I saw this on my ESXi hypervisors specifically, and I noticed it the most was when ESXi started to perform memory swapping. I was able to resolve this by increasing memory, rebooting the VM, and making sure my hypervisor wasnt swapping memory. Let me know if that helps. :)</p>
<p>Edit: I also noticed that if the underlying storage provider had poor performance, that would impact with swap data and I feel that was also am impact with sigsegv issues.</p>');insert into answers values('November',21.0,1.0,3.0,'Yes',103.0,'<p>Well like I have guessed, it is all about the compatibility issue. It is however a little unclear if this will help you solve your problem. </p>
<p>In any case, heres working example code for creating a <code>BufferedImage</code> with <code>float</code> precision:</p>
<pre><code>public class FloatImage {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        // Define dimensions and layout of the image
        int w = 300;
        int h = 200;
        int bands = 4; // 4 bands for ARGB, 3 for RGB etc
        int[] bandOffsets = {0, 1, 2, 3}; // length == bands, 0 == R, 1 == G, 2 == B and 3 == A
        // Create a TYPE_FLOAT sample model (specifying how the pixels are stored)
        SampleModel sampleModel = new PixelInterleavedSampleModel(DataBuffer.TYPE_FLOAT, w, h, bands, w  * bands, bandOffsets);
        // ...and data buffer (where the pixels are stored)
        DataBuffer buffer = new DataBufferFloat(w * h * bands);
        // Wrap it in a writable raster
        WritableRaster raster = Raster.createWritableRaster(sampleModel, buffer, null);
        // Create a color model compatible with this sample model/raster (TYPE_FLOAT)
        // Note that the number of bands must equal the number of color components in the 
        // color space (3 for RGB) + 1 extra band if the color model contains alpha 
        ColorSpace colorSpace = ColorSpace.getInstance(ColorSpace.CS_sRGB);
        ColorModel colorModel = new ComponentColorModel(colorSpace, true, false, Transparency.TRANSLUCENT, DataBuffer.TYPE_FLOAT);
        // And finally create an image with this raster
        BufferedImage image = new BufferedImage(colorModel, raster, colorModel.isAlphaPremultiplied(), null);
        System.out.println("image = " + image);
    }
}
</code></pre>
<p>For map elevation data, using a single band (<code>bands = 1; bandOffsets = {0};</code>) and a grayscale color space (<code>ColorSpace.CS_GRAY</code>) and no transparency may make more sense.</p>');insert into answers values('November',23.0,1.0,0.0,'No',1.0,'<p>I dont think that it is possible to handle basic authentication dialogs using WebDriver and thus Geb as well. List raw = null;
List&lt;?&gt; wild = raw;
// #2 (doesnt compile)
List&lt;List&gt; raw = null;
List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt; wild = raw;
</code></pre>
<p>First lets sort out why these are actually unrelated assignments. That is to say, they are defined by different rules.</p>
<p>&#35;1 is called an <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/specs/jls/se8/html/jls-5.html#jls-5.1.9" rel="nofollow"><strong>unchecked conversion</strong></a>:</p>
<blockquote>
  <p>There is an <em>unchecked conversion</em> from the raw class or interface type (<a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/specs/jls/se8/html/jls-4.html#jls-4.8" rel="nofollow">§4.8</a>) <code>G</code> to any parameterized type of the form <code>G&lt;T<sub>1</sub>,...,T<sub>n</sub>&gt;</code>.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Specifically it is a special case of an <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/specs/jls/se8/html/jls-5.html#jls-5.2" rel="nofollow"><strong>assignment context</strong></a> just for this scenario:</p>
<blockquote>
  <p>If, after [other possible conversions] have been applied, the resulting type is a raw type, an unchecked conversion may then be applied. </p>
</blockquote>
<p>&#35;2 requires a reference type conversion; however the problem with it is that it is not a <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/specs/jls/se8/html/jls-5.html#jls-5.1.5" rel="nofollow"><strong>widening conversion</strong></a> (which is the kind of reference conversion that would be implicitly allowed without a cast).</p>
<p>Why is that? Well, this is specifically governed by the <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/specs/jls/se8/html/jls-4.html#jls-4.10.2" rel="nofollow">rules of generic subtyping</a> and more specifically this bullet point:</p>
<blockquote>
  <p>Given a generic type declaration <code>C&lt;F<sub>1</sub>,...,F<sub>n</sub>&gt;</code> (<em>n</em> > 0), the <em>direct supertypes</em> of the parameterized type <code>C&lt;T<sub>1</sub>,...,T<sub>n</sub>&gt;</code>, where <code>T<sub>i</sub></code> (1 ⿤ <em>i</em> ⿤ <em>n</em>) is a type, are all of the following:</p>
  <ul>
  <li><code>C&lt;S<sub>1</sub>,...,S<sub>n</sub>&gt;</code>, where <code>S<sub>i</sub></code> contains <code>T<sub>i</sub></code> (1 ⿤ <em>i</em> ⿤ <em>n</em>).</li>
  </ul>
</blockquote>
<p>This refers us to something the JLS calls <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/specs/jls/se8/html/jls-4.html#jls-4.5.1" rel="nofollow"><strong>containment</strong></a>, where to be a valid assignment, the arguments of the left-hand side must <em>contain</em> the arguments of the right-hand side. Containment largely governs generic subtyping since <a href="http://www.angelikalanger.com/GenericsFAQ/FAQSections/ParameterizedTypes.html#FAQ101" rel="nofollow">"concrete" generic types</a> are <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/q/2745265/2891664">invariant</a>.</p>
<p>You may be familiar with the ideas that:</p>
<ul>
<li>a <code>List&lt;Dog&gt;</code> is not a <code>List&lt;Animal&gt;</code></li>
<li>but a <code>List&lt;Dog&gt;</code> is a <code>List&lt;?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;Animal&gt;</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Well, the latter is true because <code>?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;Animal</code> <em>contains</em> <code>Dog</code>.</p>
<p>So the question becomes <em>"does a List&lt;?&gt; contain a raw List"</em>? And the answer is no: although <code>List&lt;?&gt;</code> is a subtype of <code>List</code>, this relationship does not hold for type arguments.</p>
<p>There is no special rule that makes it true: <code>List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code> is not a subtype of <code>List&lt;List&gt;</code> for essentially the same reason <code>List&lt;Dog&gt;</code> is not a subtype of <code>List&lt;Animal&gt;</code>.</p>
<p>So because <code>List&lt;List&gt;</code> is not a subtype of <code>List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code>, the assignment is invalid. Similarly, you cannot perform a direct <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/specs/jls/se8/html/jls-5.html#jls-5.1.6" rel="nofollow"><strong>narrowing conversion</strong></a> cast because <code>List&lt;List&gt;</code> is not a supertype of <code>List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code> either.</p>
<hr>
<p>To make the assignment you can still apply a cast. There are two ways to do it that seem reasonable to me.</p>
<pre><code>// raw type
@SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt; list0 = (List)api();
// slightly safer
@SuppressWarnings({"unchecked", "rawtypes"})
List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt; list1 = (List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;)(List&lt;? extends List&gt;)api();
</code></pre>
<p>(You can substitute <code>JAXBElement</code> for the inner <code>List</code>.)</p>
<p>Your use-case for this casting should be safe because <code>List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code> is a more restrictive type than <code>List&lt;List&gt;</code>.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>The <em>raw type</em> statement is a widening cast then unchecked assignment. This works because, as shown above, any parameterized type can be converted to its raw type and vice-versa.</p></li>
<li><p>The <em>slightly safer</em> statement (dubbed so because it loses less type information) is a widening cast then narrowing cast. This works by casting to a common supertype:</p>
<pre><code>    List&lt;? extends List&gt;
        ⿱         ⿲
List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;     List&lt;List&gt;
</code></pre>
<p>The bounded wildcard allows the type arguments to be considered for subtyping via containment.</p>
<p><i>And as a side note, in previous revisions of this answer I was hesitant about why <code>List&lt;?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;List&gt;</code> is considered a supertype of <code>List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code>, but this can be proven through the transitive property:</i></p>
<ol>
<li><p><i><code>?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;List</code> contains <code>?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;List&lt;?&gt;</code> because <code>List</code> is a supertype of <code>List&lt;?&gt;</code>.</i></p></li>
<li><p><i><code>?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;List&lt;?&gt;</code> contains <code>List&lt;?&gt;</code>.</i></p></li>
<li><p><i>Therefore <code>?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;List</code> contains <code>List&lt;?&gt;</code>.</i></p></li>
</ol>
<p><i>That is, <code>List&lt;?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;List&gt;&nbsp;:&gt;&nbsp;List&lt;?&nbsp;extends&nbsp;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;&nbsp;:&gt;&nbsp;List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code>.</i></p></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<p>The non-technical summary here is that the specification implies that there is neither subtype nor supertype relationship between <code>List&lt;List&gt;</code> and <code>List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code>.</p>
<p>Although converting from <code>List&lt;List&gt;</code> to <code>List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code> should be <em>safe</em>, it is not allowed. (Its safe because both are a <code>List</code> that can store any kind of <code>List</code>, but a <code>List&lt;List&lt;?&gt;&gt;</code> imposes more restrictions on how its elements can be used after they are retrieved.)</p>
<p>There is unfortunately no practical reason this fails to compile except that raw types are strange and usage of them is problematic.</p>');insert into answers values('November',30.0,2.0,2.0,'No',14300.0,'<p><strong>You cannot assign or cast it directly</strong>, because raw type <code>List</code> <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/q/6783316/199048">isnt the same</a> as <code>List&lt;?&gt;</code>.</p>
<p>When using <code>List</code> type checking is ignored and you may use any generic method with any type. When using <code>List&lt;?&gt;</code> the <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/a/15518567/199048">compiler wont let you use methods with generic parameters</a>.</p>

<p>I solved it by creating and registering several dispatchers servlets with new web application contexts with different configurations (<em>RepositoryRestMvcConfiguration</em>) and a common parent which is the root application context of the Spring Boot application. To enable the API modules automatically depending on the different jars included on the classpath I emulated what Spring Boot does more or less.</p>
<p>The project is divided in several gradle modules. Something like this:</p>
<ul>
<li>project-server</li>
<li>project-api-autoconfigure</li>
<li>project-module-a-api</li>
<li>project-module-b-api</li>
<li>...</li>
<li>project-module-n-api</li>
</ul>
<p>The module <em>project-server</em> is the main one. It declares a dependency on <em>project-api-autoconfigure</em>, and at the same time it excludes the transitive dependencies of <em>project-api-autoconfigure</em> on <em>project-module-?-api module(s)</em>.</p>
<p>Inside <em>project-server.gradle</em>:</p>
<pre><code>dependencies {
    compile (project(:project-api-autoconfigure)) {
        exclude module: project-module-a-api
        exclude module: project-module-b-api
        ...
    }
    ...
}
</code></pre>
<p><em>project-api-autoconfigure</em> depends on all the API modules, so the dependencies will look like this on <em>project-api-autoconfigure.gradle</em>:</p>
<pre><code>dependencies {
    compile project(:project-module-a-api)
    compile project(:project-module-b-api)
    ...
}
</code></pre>
<p><em>project-api-autoconfigure</em> is where I create the dispatcher servlet beans with their own web application context for every API module, but this configurations are conditional on the configuration classes of every API module which live inside each API module jar.</p>
<p>I created and abstract class from which every autoconfiguration class inherit:</p>
<pre><code>public abstract class AbstractApiModuleAutoConfiguration&lt;T&gt; {
    @Autowired
    protected ApplicationContext applicationContext;
    @Autowired
    protected ServerProperties server;
    @Autowired(required = false)
    protected MultipartConfigElement multipartConfig;
    @Value("${project.rest.base-api-path}")
    protected String baseApiPath;
    protected DispatcherServlet createApiModuleDispatcherServlet() {
        AnnotationConfigWebApplicationContext webContext = new AnnotationConfigWebApplicationContext();
        webContext.setParent(applicationContext);
        webContext.register(getApiModuleConfigurationClass());
        return new DispatcherServlet(webContext);
    }
    protected ServletRegistrationBean createApiModuleDispatcherServletRegistration(DispatcherServlet apiModuleDispatcherServlet) {
        ServletRegistrationBean registration = new ServletRegistrationBean(
                apiModuleDispatcherServlet,
                this.server.getServletMapping() + baseApiPath + "/" + getApiModulePath() + "/*");
        registration.setName(getApiModuleDispatcherServletBeanName());
        if (this.multipartConfig != null) {
            registration.setMultipartConfig(this.multipartConfig);
        }
        return registration;
    }
    protected abstract String getApiModuleDispatcherServletBeanName();
    protected abstract String getApiModulePath();
    protected abstract Class&lt;T&gt; getApiModuleConfigurationClass();
}
</code></pre>
<p>So now, the autoconfiguration class for module A will look something like this:</p>
<pre><code>@Configuration
@ConditionalOnClass(ApiModuleAConfiguration.class)
@ConditionalOnProperty(prefix = "project.moduleA.", value = "enabled")
public class ApiModuleAAutoConfiguration extends AbstractApiModuleAutoConfiguration&lt;ApiModuleAConfiguration&gt; {
    public static final String API_MODULE_A_DISPATCHER_SERVLET_BEAN_NAME = "apiModuleADispatcherServlet";
    public static final String API_MODULE_A_DISPATCHER_SERVLET_REGISTRATION_BEAN_NAME = "apiModuleADispatcherServletRegistration";
    @Value("${project.moduleA.path}")
    private String apiModuleAPath;
    @Bean(name = API_MODULE_A_DISPATCHER_SERVLET_BEAN_NAME)
    public DispatcherServlet apiModuleADispatcherServlet() {
        return createApiModuleDispatcherServlet();
    }
    @Bean(name = API_MODULE_A_DISPATCHER_SERVLET_REGISTRATION_BEAN_NAME)
    public ServletRegistrationBean apiModuleADispatcherServletRegistration() {
        return createApiModuleDispatcherServletRegistration(apiModuleADispatcherServlet());
    }
    @Override
    protected String getApiModuleDispatcherServletBeanName() {
        return API_MODULE_A_DISPATCHER_SERVLET_BEAN_NAME;
    }
    @Override
    protected String getApiModulePath() {
        return apiModuleAPath;
    }
    @Override
    protected Class&lt;ApiModuleAConfiguration&gt; getApiModuleConfigurationClass() {
        return ApiModuleAConfiguration.class;
    }
}
</code></pre>
<p>And now, your <em>ApiModuleAConfiguration</em>, <em>ApiModuleBConfiguration</em>... configuration classes will be on each api module <em>project-module-a-api</em>, <em>project-module-b-api</em>...</p>
<p>They can be <em>RepositoryRestMvcConfiguration</em> or they can extend from it or they can be any other configuration class that imports the Spring Data REST configuration.</p>
<p>And last but not least, I created different gradle scripts inside the main module <em>project-server</em> to be loaded based on a property passed to gradle to emulate Maven profiles. Each script declares as dependencies the api modules that need to be included. It looks something like this:</p>
<pre><code>- project-server
    /profiles/
        profile-X.gradle
        profile-Y.gradle
        profile-Z.gradle
</code></pre>
<p>and for example, <em>profile-X</em> enables API modules A and B:</p>
<pre><code>dependencies {
    compile project(:project-module-a-api)
    compile project(:project-module-b-api)
}
processResources {
    from src/main/resources/profiles/profile-X
    include profile-x.properties
    into build/resources/main
}
</code></pre>
<p>Other profiles could enable different API modules.</p>
<p>Profiles are loaded this way from the <em>project-server.gradle</em>:</p>
<pre><code>loadProfile()
processResources {
    include **/*
    exclude profiles
}
dependencies {
        compile (project(:project-api-autoconfigure)) {
            exclude module: project-module-a-api
            exclude module: project-module-b-api
            ...
        }
        ...
    }
...
def loadProfile() {
    def profile = hasProperty(profile) ? "${profile}" : "dev"
    println "Profile: " + profile
    apply from: "profiles/" + profile + ".gradle"
}
</code></pre>
<p>And thats all more or less. I hope it helps you Jan.</p>

<pre><code>public int maxBlock(String str) {
int theEnd = str.length() - 1;
int[] arrayHolder = new int[10];
int count = 0;
int arrayCount = 0;
if (str.length() == 0) return 0;
for (int i = 0; i &lt; str.length(); i++){
  if (i == theEnd){
      // Do Nothing
  } 
  else if (str.charAt(i) == str.charAt(i+1)){
      count++;
  }
  else if (count &gt; 0){
      arrayHolder[arrayCount] = count + 1;
      arrayCount++;
      count = 0;

}
arrayHolder[arrayCount] = count + 1;
int theGreatest = 0;
for (int i = 0; i &lt; arrayHolder.length; i++){
  if (arrayHolder[i] &gt; theGreatest){
      theGreatest = arrayHolder[i];
  }
}

<pre><code>    public int maxBlock(String str) {
       if(str.length() == 0){
       return 0;
       } 
       int biggest = Integer.MIN_VALUE;
       for(int a = 0; a &lt; str.length(); a++){
       if((countBlock(str, str.substring(a, a + 1), a) &gt; biggest)){
       biggest = (countBlock(str, str.substring(a, a + 1), a));
       }
       }
       return biggest; //by now we have the biggest
    }

       for(int a = startIndex + 1; a &lt; s.length(); a++){ //start right after index
       if(s.substring(a, a + 1).contains(any)){ //keep going
       cnt++;
       }

       }
